        </div><div class="casAbstract">Aq. zinc-ion batteries (ZIBs) have triggered a great deal of scientific research and become a promising alternative for large-scale energy storage applications, owing to the unique merits of high volumetric energy d., abundance of zinc resources, eco-friendliness, and safety.  The pace of progress of ZIB development, however, is hindered by their poor reversibility and sluggish kinetics, derived from the dissoln. of active materials in aq. electrolytes and the strong electrostatic interactions between Zn2+ and the cathode lattice.  Herein, a vanadium oxide (V2O5-x)/polyaniline (PANI-V) superlattice structure is demonstrated as a model of superlattice structural engineering to overcome these weaknesses.  In this superlattice, the PANI layer not only plays the role of a spacer to expand the V2O5-x interlayer spacing but also serves as a conductive capacity contributor.  Moreover, the PANI layer servers as structural stabilizer to restrain the dissoln. of V2O5-x active materials in aq. electrolytes.  In addn., it introduces an interface effect to modulate the charge distribution of the V2O5-x monolayer, promoting Zn-ion diffusion into the structure.  Correspondingly, weakening the electrostatic interactions and suppressing the active materials dissoln. synergistically boosts the electrochem. performance for Zn-ion storage.  This work paves the way for the development/improvement of cathodes for aq. zinc-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo58cbjE89UwrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhAyiuL_XuUpA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXitlaitr%252FP&amp;md5=0f319a65e5476f5c427a8cab938bc007</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202001633"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bak, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shadike, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Waluyo, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hunt, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Senanayake, S.                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The Role of Electron Localization in Covalency and Electrochemical Properties of Lithium-Ion Battery Cathode Materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xuelong; Fan, Xiulin; Yu, Xiqian; Bak, Seongmin; Shadike, Zulipiya; Waluyo, Iradwikanari; Hunt, Adrian; Senanayake, Sanjaya D.; Li, Hong; Chen, Liquan; Wang, Chunsheng; Xiao, Ruijuan; Hu, Enyuan; Yang, Xiao-Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Following the fundamental research conducted by J.B. Goodenough, the important role of electron localization induced by elemental substitution is studied.  The size and electron negativity of host and substituting ions are two important factors in tuning material properties such as local structure and transition metal (TM) oxygen covalency.  However, another factor, electron localization, which is widely studied in catalyst research but largely overlooked for battery materials, deserves systematic studies.  A combined investigation using synchrotronbased X-ray spectroscopy and theor. calcns. is carried out on the Li-Co-Mn-O model system in which the substituting cation Mn4+, with its 3d3 electronic structure, is used as a promoter for electron localization.  Results indicate that electron localization greatly influences the Co-O bond by making it less covalent, which increases the delithiation voltage.  It is also found that during charge/discharge, electron localization tends to make TM K-edge X-ray absorption near edge spectroscopy (XANES) spectra show a more ''rigid shift'' behavior while electron delocalization makes the XANES exhibit a ''shape change.''.  It clearly explains why the K-edge XANES data of some TM oxides show no ''rigid shift'' while the nominal valence states changed.  This work highlights the importance of electron localization with guidance for XANES interpretation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqSCkyH3pYr-bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljQRo15izIKiA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXptlelsLg%253D&amp;md5=88aa5b3b59ba70a8f04749394d21e1a6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1038/s41563-018-0098-1"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Aubrey, M.                         cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electron delocalization and charge mobility as a function of reduction in a metal-organic framework</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Aubrey, Michael L.; Wiers, Brian M.; Andrews, Sean C.; Sakurai, Tsuneaki; Reyes-Lillo, Sebastian E.; Hamed, Samia M.; Yu, Chung-Jui; Darago, Lucy E.; Mason, Jarad A.; Baeg, Jin-Ook; Grandjean, Fernande; Long, Gary J.; Seki, Shu; Neaton, Jeffrey B.; Yang, Peidong; Long, Jeffrey R.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Conductive metal-org. frameworks are an emerging class of three-dimensional architectures with degrees of modularity, synthetic flexibility and structural predictability that are unprecedented in other porous materials.  However, engendering long-range charge delocalization and establishing synthetic strategies that are broadly applicable to the diverse range of structures encountered for this class of materials remain challenging.  Here, we report the synthesis of KxFe2(BDP)3 (0 ≤ x ≤ 2; BDP2- = 1,4-benzenedipyrazolate), which exhibits full charge delocalization within the parent framework and charge mobilities comparable to technol. relevant polymers and ceramics.  Through a battery of spectroscopic methods, computational techniques and single-microcrystal field-effect transistor measurements, we demonstrate that fractional redn. of Fe2(BDP)3 results in a metal-org. framework that displays a nearly 10,000-fold enhancement in cond. along a single crystallog. axis.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Heteroatomic interface engineering in MOF-derived carbon heterostructures with built-in electric-field effects for high performance Al-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Caixia; Dong, Shihua; Tang, Rui; Ge, Xiaoli; Zhang, Zhiwei; Wang, Chengxiang; Lu, Yupeng; Yin, Longwei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3201-3211</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Confronted with challenges in promoting fast AlxCly- anion diffusion and intercalation for aluminum ion batteries (AIBs), it is of vital importance to rationally design gradient hetero-interfaces with an ideal built-in interfacial elec. potential to enhance charge diffusion and transfer kinetics.  Herein, we demonstrate an effective strategy to realize accurate tuning gradient heteroatom N and P doping in MOF-derived porous carbon in C@N-C@N,P-C graded heterostructures.  Importantly, gradient N and P doping could modify the electronic structure of MOF-derived carbon as certified by DFT calcns., and lead to charge redistribution to induce graded energy levels and a built-in elec. field in the C@N-C@N,P-C graded heteroat. interface, thus boosting interfacial charge transfer and accelerating reaction kinetics.  Furthermore, the large surface area and high porosity of C@N-C@N,P-C graded heterostructures could efficiently absorb electrolyte and enhance anion transport kinetics.  As expected, the designed gradiently N,P-doped C@N-C@N,P-C heterostructure with a built-in interfacial elec. field could facilitate electron and AlCl4- anion transfer spontaneously between N,P-C, N-C and C gradient components, exhibiting a superior capacity of 98 mA h g-1 at a high c.d. of 5 A g-1 after 2500 cycles.  This strategy reveals new insights about the gradient energy band for designing high-performance electrochem. energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGobGGlq3OiNm7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljQRo15izIKiA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Built-in oriented electric field facilitating durable Zn-MnO2 battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lian, Sitian; Sun, Congli; Xu, Weina; Huo, Wangchen; Luo, Yanzhu; Zhao, Kangning; Yao, Guang; Xu, Wangwang; Zhang, Yuxin; Li, Zhi; Yu, Kesong; Zhao, Hongbin; Cheng, Hongwei; Zhang, Jiujun; Mai, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">62</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">79-84</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable aq. zinc ion batteries are particularly attractive for large-scale application due to their features including low cost, environmental friendliness, and safety.  Herein, we report the use of defect engineering to generate oxygen vacancies in tunneled α-MnO2 through surface gradient Ti doping for long-life Zn-MnO2 battery.  Interestingly, the introduction of surface gradient Ti doping leads to shrinkage of the interlayer, but simultaneously generates oxygen vacancies as compensated by electron due to the decreased valence state of Mn.  Moreover, Ti substitution as well as the created oxygen vacancies open the [MnO6] octahedral walls and result in imbalanced charge distribution and local elec. field in the crystal structure, accelerating ion/electron migration rates.  Thus, diffusion coeffs. of both Zn2+ and H+ ions in Ti-MnO2 nanowires are improved.  Consequently, the Ti-MnO2 nanowires show improved both H+ and Zn2+ ions storage capacity in Zn/MnO2 battery and achieved excellent high-rate capability and ultralong cycling stability with a low capacity decay rate of 0.005% per cycle at high rate of 1 A g-1.  It is believed that the intentionally created vacancies in this work opens up approaches to enhance existing materials that may have applications in more efficient and durable multi-valent ion battery and other technologies.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGogQbvEGv8my7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljQRo15izIKiA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Interfacial coupled design of epitaxial Graphene@SiC Schottky junction with built-in electric field for high-performance anodes of lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Changlong; Wang, Yan-Jie; Gu, Hao; Fan, Hongbo; Yang, Guanjun; Ignaszak, Anna; Tang, Xiaofu; Liu, Dan; Zhang, Jiujun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">77</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">105092</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In-situ epitaxial graphene (EG) strategy is adopted to activate the electrochem. inactive silicon carbide (SiC) by constructing Schottky junction for high-performance anode of lithium-ion battery (LIB).  Raman and Hall measurements confirm the high quality and electronic mobility of EG.  Refined structural characterization (XPS and XANES) and theor. anal. indicate that the interfacial coupled structure exhibits Schottky junction with an inherent built-in elec. field, and the strong interfacial Si-C interaction could reinforce the interfacial coupling.  This prototype can systematically comprehend interfacial electronic properties and transport mechanisms.  As a proof-of-concept study, this interfacially designed Schottky junction is demonstrated to promote both the surface electron densities and charge carriers transportation efficiency for LIB anodes.  Even at 10.0 A g-1, the EG@SiC anode can still deliver a capacity of 322.1 mA h g-1.  The ex-situ XRD, HRTEM, and XPS anal. confirm the reversible intercalation reaction mechanism and excellent structural stability.  The proposed strategy of constructing Schottky junction through interlayer engineering can construct advanced SiC-based electrodes for high-performance rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGotu7Qu_QI5PbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8k3j6p6ckpQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Covalent Coupling-Stabilized Transition-Metal Sulfide/Carbon Nanotube Composites for Lithium/Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hou, Tianyi; Liu, Borui; Sun, Xiaohong; Fan, Anran; Xu, Zhongkai; Cai, Shu; Zheng, Chunming; Yu, Guihua; Tricoli, Antonio</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6735-6746</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition-metal sulfides (TMSs) powered by conversion and/or alloying reactions are considered to be promising anode materials for advanced lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, the limited electronic cond. and large vol. expansion severely hinder their practical application.  Herein, we report a covalent coupling strategy for TMS-based anode materials using amide linkages to bind TMSs and carbon nanotubes (CNTs).  In the synthesis, the thiourea acts as not only the capping agent for morphol. control but also the linking agent for the covalent coupling.  As a proof of concept, the covalently coupled ZnS/CNT composite (CC-ZnS/CNT) has been prepd., with ZnS nanoparticles (~ 10 nm) tightly anchored on CNT bundles.  The compact ZnS-CNT heterojunctions are greatly beneficial to facilitating the electron/ion transfer and ensuring structural stability.  Due to the strong coupling interaction between ZnS and CNTs, the composite presents prominent pseudocapacitive behavior and highly reversible electrochem. processes, thus leading to superior long-term stability and excellent rate capability, delivering reversible capacities of 333 mAh g-1 at 2 A g-1 over 4000 cycles for LIBs and 314 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1 after 500 cycles for SIBs.  Consequently, CC-ZnS/CNT exhibits great competence for applications in LIBs and SIBs, and the covalent coupling strategy is proposed as a promising approach for designing high-performance anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpZBw1KdNa61bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8k3j6p6ckpQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXmvVCksr8%253D&amp;md5=dd6faf5db1e47beb94071541b2892f8e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201703028"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tai, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sencadas, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Konstantinov, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Advanced Sodium Ion Battery Anode Constructed via Chemical Bonding between Phosphorus, Carbon Nanotube, and Cross-Linked Polymer Binder</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Song, Jiangxuan; Yu, Zhaoxin; Gordin, Mikhail L.; Li, Xiaolin; Peng, Huisheng; Wang, Donghai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Maintaining structural stability is a great challenge for high-capacity conversion electrodes with large vol. change but is necessary for the development of high-energy-d., long-cycling batteries.  Here, a stable phosphorus anode is reported for sodium ion batteries by the synergistic use of chem. bonded phosphorus-carbon nanotube (P-CNT) hybrid and cross-linked polymer binder.  The P-CNT hybrid was synthesized through ball-milling of red phosphorus and carboxylic group functionalized carbon nanotubes.  The P-O-C bonds formed in this process help maintain contact between phosphorus and CNTs, leading to a durable hybrid.  In addn., cross-linked CM-cellulose-citric acid binder was used to form a robust electrode.  As a result, this anode delivers a stable cycling capacity of 1586.2 mAh/g after 100 cycles, along with high initial Coulombic efficiency of 84.7% and subsequent cycling efficiency of ∼99%.  The unique electrode framework through chem. bonding strategy reported here is potentially inspirable for other electrode materials with large vol. change in use.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoS4Pq1G8HaQrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8k3j6p6ckpQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhslWjsb7E&amp;md5=7aa0ddefccdd71c9a74a5848ed1dbe6e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202002298"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xi, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Duan, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sandwich Structures Constructed by ZnSe–N-C@MoSe 2 Located in Graphene for Efficient Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sandwich structures constructed by ZnSe⊂N-C@MoSe2 Located in graphene for efficient sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shi, Nianxiang; Chu, Yanting; Xi, Baojuan; Huang, Man; Chen, Weihua; Duan, Bin; Zhang, Chenghui; Feng, Jinkui; Xiong, Shenglin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">41</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hybrid hierarchical micro/nanostructures possess great potential in engineering of advanced electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Herein, a sandwich hierarchical architecture composed of ZnSe nanoparticles fastened in N-doped carbon polyhedra anchoring onto graphene with the modification of MoSe2 nanosheets (ZnSe⊂N-C@MoSe2/rGO) is synthesized by a self-template and subsequent selenization strategy.  Due to the distinctive architectural and multicompositional features, these hybrids deliver a high reversible capacity of 319.4 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 for 1800 cycles, 206.5 mA h g-1 at 6 A g-1 for 2800 cycles, and 177.7 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1 for 5000 cycles, as well as a better rate capability up to 10 A g-1 with a reversible capacity of 224.4 mAh g-1 as an anode material for SIBs.  By comparing the capacity contribution, electrochem. impedance spectra and DNa+ of different materials, the advantages of ZnSe⊂N-C@MoSe2/rGO are confirmed.  The sodium storage mechanism of hybrids is further revealed by in situ X-ray diffraction patterns and high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy results.  The improved sodium storage properties of hybrids manifest the significance of elaborate construction of novel multicomponent hierarchical architectures with higher complexity.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo3KMObSzX9arVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8k3j6p6ckpQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhvVGgsLzL&amp;md5=dddc9adb82cc51a2dc6b5c1763ce1e9e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.9b11861"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">You, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pei, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Che, R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Self-assembly-magnetized MXene avoid dual-agglomeration with enhanced interfaces for strong microwave absorption through a tunable electromagnetic property</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-Assembly-Magnetized MXene Avoid Dual-Agglomeration with Enhanced Interfaces for Strong Microwave Absorption through a Tunable Electromagnetic Property</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Xiao; You, Wenbin; Wang, Lei; Liu, Jiwei; Wu, Zhengchen; Pei, Ke; Li, Yuesheng; Che, Renchao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Multilayered microwave absorbers which can provide massive interfaces are highly needed for electromagnetic-wave absorption properties enhancement.  Meanwhile, how to effectively avoid agglomeration and further widen the absorption band is still a challenge.  Herein, accordion-like magnetized MXene/Ni composites were fabricated by the electrostatic self-assembly interaction between multilayer MXene and Ni(OH)2 nanoplates and subsequent in situ redn. in H2/Ar atms.  Ni nanoparticles were uniformly distributed without magnetic agglomeration between the multilayered gaps of the adjacent 2-dimensional (2 dimension) MXene (Ti3C2Tx) of MXene/Ni nanocomposites (magnetized MXene), which holds the distinct absorption performance that the reflection loss max. measure up -50.5 dB at 5.5 GHz.  Also, dynamic magnetic response of magnetized MXene absorber was firstly researched by the electron holog. anal.  The related key mechanism includes the enhanced magnetic loss, less dual agglomeration (multilayer MXene itself and magnetic agglomeration), more interfaces and intrinsic defects for related polarization.  Broadened absorption bandwidth can further be obtained by changing the mass ratio of MXene to Ni that possesses the widest absorption bandwidth of 5.28 GHz.  This work provides a new route for the balance among strong absorption intensity, tunable electromagnetic properties and wide absorption bandwidth of the MXene-based nanocomposites.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGry6rv8_eYncbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8k3j6p6ckpQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metal-Semiconductor Phase Twinned Hierarchical MoS2 Nanowires with Expanded Interlayers for Sodium-Ion Batteries with Ultralong Cycle Life</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ye, Wei; Wu, Fangfang; Shi, Nianxiang; Zhou, Han; Chi, Qianqian; Chen, Weihua; Du, Shiyu; Gao, Peng; Li, Haibo; Xiong, Shenglin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered a prospective candidate for large-scale energy storage due to the merits of abundant sodium resources and low cost.  However, a lack of suitable advanced anode materials has hindered further applications.  Herein, metal-semiconductor mixed phase twinned hierarchical (MPTH) MoS2 nanowires with an expanded interlayer (9.63 Å) are engineered and prepd. using MoO3 nanobelts as a self-sacrificed template in the presence of a trace amt. of (NH4)6Mo7O24·4H2O as initiator.  The greatly expanded interlayer spacing accelerates Na+ insertion/extn. kinetics, and the metal-semiconductor mixed phase enhances electron transfer ability and stabilizes electrode structure during cycling.  Benefiting from the structural merits, the MPTH MoS2 electrode delivers high reversible capacities of 200 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 for 200 cycles and 154 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 for 2450 cycles in the voltage range of 0.4-3.0 V.  Strikingly, the electrode maintains 6500 cycles at a c.d. of 2 A g-1, corresponding to a capacity retention of 82.8% of the 2nd cycle, overwhelming the all reported MoS2 cycling results.  This study provides an alternative strategy to boost SIB cycling performance in terms of reversible capacity by virtue of interlayer expansion and structure stability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGppq1pGfamQ6LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li4Azc5J3fVsg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fabrication of SnS2/Mn2SnS4/Carbon Heterostructures for Sodium-Ion Batteries with High Initial Coulombic Efficiency and Cycling Stability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ou, Xing; Cao, Liang; Liang, Xinghui; Zheng, Fenghua; Zheng, Hong-Sheng; Yang, Xianfeng; Wang, Jeng-Han; Yang, Chenghao; Liu, Meilin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">SnS2 has been extensive studied as an anode material for sodium storage owing to its high theor. specific capacity, whereas the unsatisfied initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) caused by the partial irreversible conversion reaction during the charge/discharge process is one of the crit. issues that hamper its practical applications.  Hence, heterostructured SnS2/Mn2SnS4/carbon nanoboxes (SMS/C NBs) have been developed by a facial wet-chem. method and utilized as the anode material of sodium ion batteries.  SMS/C NBs can deliver an initial capacity of 841.2 mAh g-1 with high ICE of 90.8%, excellent rate capability (752.3, 604.7, 570.1, 546.9, 519.7, and 488.7 mAh g-1 at the current rate of 0.1, 0.5, 1.0, 2.0, 5.0, and 10.0 A g-1, resp.), and long cycling stability (522.5 mAh g-1 at 5.0 A g-1 after 500 cycles).  The existence of SnS2/Mn2SnS4 heterojunctions can effectively stabilize the reaction products Sn and Na2S, greatly prevent the coarsening of nanosized Sn0, and enhance reversible conversion--alloying reaction, which play a key role in improving the ICE and extending the cycling performance.  Moreover, the heterostructured SMS coupled with the interacting carbon network provides efficient channels for electrons and Na+ diffusion, resulting in an excellent rate performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpbZ1R4cwpT7rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li4Azc5J3fVsg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXjsVaqu7Y%253D&amp;md5=4575ad64469267af9d8a39c2100599e4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1002/ange.201510978"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Boosted Charge Transfer in SnS/SnO 2 Heterostructures: Toward High Rate Capability for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Monolayer atomic crystal molecular superlattices</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Chen; He, Qiyuan; Halim, Udayabagya; Liu, Yuanyue; Zhu, Enbo; Lin, Zhaoyang; Xiao, Hai; Duan, Xidong; Feng, Ziying; Cheng, Rui; Weiss, Nathan O.; Ye, Guojun; Huang, Yun-Chiao; Wu, Hao; Cheng, Hung-Chieh; Shakir, Imran; Liao, Lei; Chen, Xianhui; Goddard, William A., III; Huang, Yu; Duan, Xiangfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature (London, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">555</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7695</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">231-236</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NATUAS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0028-0836</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Research</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Artificial superlattices, based on van der Waals heterostructures of two-dimensional at. crystals such as graphene or molybdenum disulfide, offer technol. opportunities beyond the reach of existing materials.  Typical strategies for creating such artificial superlattices rely on arduous layer-by-layer exfoliation and restacking, with limited yield and reproducibility.  The bottom-up approach of using chem.-vapor deposition produces high-quality heterostructures but becomes increasingly difficult for high-order superlattices.  The intercalation of selected two-dimensional at. crystals with alkali metal ions offers an alternative way to superlattice structures, but these usually have poor stability and seriously altered electronic properties.  Here we report an electrochem. mol. intercalation approach to a new class of stable superlattices in which monolayer at. crystals alternate with mol. layers.  Using black phosphorus as a model system, we show that intercalation with cetyl-trimethylammonium bromide produces monolayer phosphorene mol. superlattices in which the interlayer distance is more than double that in black phosphorus, effectively isolating the phosphorene monolayers.  Elec. transport studies of transistors fabricated from the monolayer phosphorene mol. superlattice show an on/off current ratio exceeding 107, along with excellent mobility and superior stability.  We further show that several different two-dimensional at. crystals, such as molybdenum disulfide and tungsten diselenide, can be intercalated with quaternary ammonium mols. of varying sizes and symmetries to produce a broad class of superlattices with tailored mol. structures, interlayer distances, phase compns., electronic and optical properties.  These studies define a versatile material platform for fundamental studies and potential technol. applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoSOY4lYQBoY7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li4Azc5J3fVsg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXktFKqtbs%253D&amp;md5=293778dfa8c4fdc0a9104a1523397cab</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1038/s41467-017-01149-4"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wan, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kondou, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zong, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Koumoto, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrahigh thermoelectric power factor in flexible hybrid inorganic-organic superlattice</span>. <i>Nat. Commun.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1024</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/s41467-017-01149-4</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D8%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D1024%26journal%3DNat.%2BCommun.%26author%3DC.%2BWan%26author%3DR.%2BTian%26author%3DM.%2BKondou%26author%3DR.%2BYang%26author%3DP.%2BZong%26author%3DK.%2BKoumoto%26title%3DUltrahigh%2Bthermoelectric%2Bpower%2Bfactor%2Bin%2Bflexible%2Bhybrid%2Binorganic-organic%2Bsuperlattice%26doi%3D10.1038%252Fs41467-017-01149-4&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.2c01009&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fs41467-017-01149-4&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrahigh thermoelectric power factor in flexible hybrid inorganic-organic superlattice</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wan Chunlei; Zong Pengan; Tian Ruoming; Koumoto Kunihito; Kondou Mami; Yang Ronggui; Yang Ronggui; Yang Ronggui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1024</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Hybrid inorganic-organic superlattice with an electron-transmitting but phonon-blocking structure has emerged as a promising flexible thin film thermoelectric material.  However, the substantial challenge in optimizing carrier concentration without disrupting the superlattice structure prevents further improvement of the thermoelectric performance.  Here we demonstrate a strategy for carrier optimization in a hybrid inorganic-organic superlattice of TiS2[tetrabutylammonium] x [hexylammonium] y , where the organic layers are composed of a random mixture of tetrabutylammonium and hexylammonium molecules.  By vacuum heating the hybrid materials at an intermediate temperature, the hexylammonium molecules with a lower boiling point are selectively de-intercalated, which reduces the electron density due to the requirement of electroneutrality.  The tetrabutylammonium molecules with a higher boiling point remain to support and stabilize the superlattice structure.  The carrier concentration can thus be effectively reduced, resulting in a remarkably high power factor of 904 μW m(-1) K(-2) at 300 K for flexible thermoelectrics, approaching the values achieved in conventional inorganic semiconductors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcSx3YrIaaucHty3lHz94U-GfW6udTcc2eYXXg0EcBolzrntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC1M7hvFSgsw%253D%253D&amp;md5=477248318f5892e4de6ac36ab16db1c9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1039/d0ee03206a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sasaki, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Two-dimensional organic-inorganic superlattice-like heterostructures for energy storage applications</span>. <i>Energy Environ. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">4834</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">4853</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/d0ee03206a</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D13%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D4834-4853%26journal%3DEnergy%2BEnviron.%2BSci.%26author%3DP.%2BXiong%26author%3DY.%2BWu%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DR.%2BMa%26author%3DT.%2BSasaki%26author%3DX.%2BWang%26author%3DJ.%2BZhu%26title%3DTwo-dimensional%2Borganic-inorganic%2Bsuperlattice-like%2Bheterostructures%2Bfor%2Benergy%2Bstorage%2Bapplications%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fd0ee03206a&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.2c01009&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fd0ee03206a&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Two-dimensional organic-inorganic superlattice-like heterostructures for energy storage applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiong, Pan; Wu, Yunyan; Liu, Yifan; Ma, Renzhi; Sasaki, Takayoshi; Wang, Xin; Zhu, Junwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4834-4853</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Two-dimensional (2D) superlattices, assembled from vertically stacked inorg. 2D nanosheets, are a new class of artificial 2D materials of significant scientific and technol. importance.  The incorporation of an infinite no. of org. mols. within these systems further provides unlimited possibilities for the design and synthesis of 2D org.-inorg. hybrid superlattices with predictable functionalities.  Herein, the recent research progress in 2D org.-inorg. hybrid superlattices is summarized.  Many facile strategies have been developed for the fabrication of 2D org.-inorg. hybrid superlattices, in which continuous org. layers are intercalated in the interlayer galleries of inorg. 2D nanosheets at an at./mol. scale.  The advantages of these 2D superlattices are discussed for some typical energy storage applications, such as supercapacitors, lithium/sodium/potassium ion batteries, and multivalent-ion rechargeable batteries.  The challenges and perspectives for future research are also outlined.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqeuk91SO64DbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgjIiM2SZSBOA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXit1aku7nN&amp;md5=8f46520c50026cd4340477f6bd4a88ff</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.7b08522"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sakai, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sasaki, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Genuine unilamellar metal oxide nanosheets confined in a superlattice-like structure for superior energy storage</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1768</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1777</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Genuine Unilamellar Metal Oxide Nanosheets Confined in a Superlattice-like Structure for Superior Energy Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiong, Pan; Ma, Renzhi; Sakai, Nobuyuki; Sasaki, Takayoshi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-dimensional (2D) metal oxide nanosheets can exhibit exceptional electrochem. performance owing to their shortened ion diffusion distances, abundant active sites, and various valence states.  Esp., genuine unilamellar nanosheets with an at.-scale thickness are expected to exhibit the ultimate energy storage capability but have not yet achieved their potential.  Here, we demonstrate the use of genuine unilamellar MnO2 nanosheets for high-performance Li and Na storage using an alternately stacked MnO2/graphene superlattice-like structure.  Different from previous reports, all unilamellar MnO2 nanosheets are sepd. and stabilized between the graphene monolayers, resulting in highly reversible 2D-confined conversion processes.  As a consequence, large specific capacities of 1325 and 795 mAh/g at 0.1 A/g, high-rate capacities of 370 and 245 mAh/g at 12.8 A/g, and excellent cycling stabilities after 5000 cycles with ∼0.004 and 0.0078% capacity decay per cycle were obtained for Li and Na storage, resp., presenting the best reported performance to date.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrBywobvH6cI7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgjIiM2SZSBOA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXht1yms7w%253D&amp;md5=ff3cf056b69f587984fbe74c485df9af</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1021/acsenergylett.8b00110"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sakai, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nurdiwijayanto, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sasaki, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Unilamellar Metallic MoS2/Graphene Superlattice for Efficient Sodium Storage and Hydrogen Evolution</span>. <i>ACS Energy Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">997</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1005</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unilamellar Metallic MoS2/Graphene Superlattice for Efficient Sodium Storage and Hydrogen Evolution</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiong, Pan; Ma, Renzhi; Sakai, Nobuyuki; Nurdiwijayanto, Leanddas; Sasaki, Takayoshi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">997-1005</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Unilamellar metallic nanosheets possess superiority for electrochem. energy storage and conversion applications compared to the few-layered bulk and semiconducting counterparts.  Here, we report the utilization of unilamellar metallic 1T phase MoS2 nanosheets for efficient sodium storage and hydrogen evolution through a MoS2/graphene superlattice.  The superlattice-like assembly composed of alternately restacked unilamellar MoS2 and modified reduced graphene oxide nanosheets was prepd. by a facile soln.-phase direct restacking method.  As an anode for sodium storage, the MoS2/graphene superlattice anode exhibited an excellent rate capability of ∼240 mA h g-1 at 51.2 A g-1 and a stable reversible capacity of ∼380 mA h g-1 after 1000 cycles at 10 A g-1.  In addn., a low onset potential of ∼88 mV and a small Tafel slope of 48.7 mV decade-1 were attained for the hydrogen evolution reaction.  Our findings are important for further developing the potential of 2D nanosheets for energy storage and conversion.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoA1NWsuB-9RLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgjIiM2SZSBOA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXlt1Sjtbo%253D&amp;md5=c836f9f123cfdea7d82934cae6dc8d4c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.05.012"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Robles Hernandez, F.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhancing sodium-ion battery performance with interlayer-expanded MoS2-PEO nanocomposites</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yifei; Liang, Yanliang; Robles Hernandez, Francisco C.; Deog Yoo, Hyun; An, Qinyou; Yao, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The larger ionic radius of Na ion (1.06 Å) compared with that of Li ion (0.76 Å) is a fundamental reason for the inferior diffusion kinetics of Na ion in intercalation hosts.  Here we report interlayer expansion of intercalation hosts as a general strategy to facilitate the solid-state diffusion of Na ions.  Based on this strategy, poly(ethylene oxide)-intercalated MoS2 composites (PEO-MoS2) were synthesized via a facile exfoliation-restacking method and tested as anode materials for Na-ion batteries (NIBs).  The interlayer spacing of MoS2 was increased from 0.615 nm to 1.45 nm by insertion of controlled amts. of PEO.  The bilayer PEO-intercalated MoS2 composite (PEO2L-MoS2) exhibits a specific capacity of 225 mA h g-1 under a c.d. of 50 mA g-1, twice as high as that of com. MoS2 (com-MoS2), and shows improved rate performance due to enhanced Na-ion diffusivity.  The improvement in the electrochem. performance demonstrates that interlayer expansion is an effective strategy for the development of high performance electrode materials for battery technologies based on the storage of large ions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPDeJY5F5U6rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgjIiM2SZSBOA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXptFGhu7w%253D&amp;md5=2ff5dbb1e1ec86fba37e45f24a07c7f9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201705788"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xi, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical Porous Nanosheets Constructed by Graphene-Coated, Interconnected TiO2 Nanoparticles for Ultrafast Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Quantum-Matter Bi/THeterostructure Embedded in N-Doped Porous Carbon Nanosheets for Enhanced Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Man; Xi, Baojuan; Shi, Nianxiang; Feng, Jinkui; Qian, Yitai; Xue, Dongfeng; Xiong, Shenglin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small Structures</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Combining the strength of heterostructure engineering with the properties of quantum materials, quantum-scale heterostructure will open up a new stage for material design.  Herein, a kind of anode material with heterostructures made of Bi/TiO2 quantum dots embedded into N-doped carbon nanosheets (Bi/TiO2 HQDs⊂NC) is reported.  Importantly, unique electronic states, structural distortions and defects, and functionalities can be integrated in the quantum-scale heterostructure, giving rise to opportunities for reducing the ion-diffusion resistance and facilitating interfacial charge transport at interface during the storage process.  The integrated design greatly reduces the migration energy barrier of Na+, promotes the electron/Na+ transportation, buffers the vol. variation of electrodes upon cycling, heightens the elec. cond. and electrochem. reactivity of the hybrids, and provides rich active interfacial sites for sodium uptake.  Due to these merits, these Bi/TiO2 HQDs⊂NC hybrid nanosheets manifest excellent sodium storage properties in terms of a high reversible capacity of 299.1 at 0.2 A g-1 with an ultrahigh rate capability up to 20 A g-1 with a capacity of 132.7 mAh g-1 and an ultralong cycle life over 10 000 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrWWf98OBaxS7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgjIiM2SZSBOA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen and fluorine co-doped TiO2/carbon microspheres for advanced anodes in sodium-ion batteries: High volumetric capacity, superior power density and large areal capacity</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lv, Dan; Wang, Dongdong; Wang, Nana; Liu, Hongxia; Zhang, Shaojie; Zhu, Yansong; Song, Kepeng; Yang, Jian; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Energy Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">68</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Science Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Fast charging and high volumetric capacity are two of the crit. demands for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Although nanostructured materials achieve outstanding rate performance, they suffer from low tap d. and small volumetric capacity.  Therefore, how to realize large volumetric capacity and high tap d. simultaneously is very challenging.  Here, N/F co-doped TiO2/carbon microspheres (NF-TiO2/C) are synthesized to achieve both of them.  Theor. calcns. reveal that N and F co-doping increases the contents of oxygen vacancies and narrows the bandgaps of TiO2 and C, improving the electronic cond. of NF-TiO2/C.  Furthermore, NF-TiO2/C exhibits the high binding energy and low diffusion energy barrier of Na+, significantly facilitating Na+ storage and Na+ diffusion.  Therefore, NF-TiO2/C offers a high tap d. (1.51 g cm-3), an outstanding rate performance (∼125.9 mAh g-1 at 100 C), a large volumetric capacity (∼190 mAh cm-3 at 100 C), a high areal capacity (∼4.8 mAh cm-2) and an ultra-long cycling performance (∼80.2% after 10,000 cycles at 10 C) simultaneously.  In addn., NF-TiO2/C||Na3V2(PO4)3 full cells achieve an ultrahigh power d. of 25.2 kW kg-1.  These results indicate the great promise of NF-TiO2/C as a high-volumetric-capacity and high-power-d. anode material of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrHVu7UjTFaQ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li0e6M8u2dzIg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XisFOju7jM&amp;md5=c3571797aa78b29e05d08e8a4409d6dc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b03270"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Porter, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Boron-Doped Anatase TiO2 as a High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Baofeng; Zhao, Fei; Du, Guodong; Porter, Spencer; Liu, Yong; Zhang, Peng; Cheng, Zhenxiang; Liu, Hua Kun; Huang, Zhenguo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pristine and boron-doped anatase TiO2 were prepd. via a facile sol-gel method and the hydrothermal method for application as anode materials in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  The sol-gel method leads to agglomerated TiO2, whereas the hydrothermal method is conducive to the formation of highly cryst. and discrete nanoparticles.  The structure, morphol., and electrochem. properties were studied.  The crystal size of TiO2 with boron doping is smaller than that of the nondoped crystals, which indicates that the addn. of boron can inhibit the crystal growth.  The electrochem. measurements demonstrated that the reversible capacity of the B-doped TiO2 is higher than that for the pristine sample.  B-doping also effectively enhances the rate performance.  The capacity of the B-doped TiO2 could reach 150 mAh/g at the high current rate of 2C and the capacity decay is only about 8 mAh/g over 400 cycles.  The remarkable performance could be attributed to the lattice expansion resulting from B doping and the shortened Li+ diffusion distance due to the nanosize.  These results indicate that B-doped TiO2 can be a good candidate for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqa4lL9nW9zibVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li0e6M8u2dzIg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xpt1aruro%253D&amp;md5=d6d050542c7f7e1438212730be56e3df</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1021/am501772a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oh, S.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, J.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yoon, C.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Overcoming Ion Transport Barrier by Plasma Heterointerface Engineering: Epitaxial Titanium Carbonitride on Nitrogen-Doped TiO2 for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cai, Qianli; Li, Xinglong; Hu, Ertao; Wang, Zhongyue; Lv, Peng; Zheng, Jiajin; Yu, Kehan; Wei, Wei; Ostrikov, Kostya</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">18</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">16</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2200694</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Anatase TiO2 is a promising anode material for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its high specific capacity, low cost, and excellent cycle stability.  However, low elec. cond. and poor Na+ ion transport in TiO2 limit its practical applications.  Here, substantially boosted Na+ ion transport and charge transfer kinetics are demonstrated by constructing a near-ideal non-rectifying titanium carbon nitride/nitrogen-doped TiO2 (TiCxN1-x/N-TiO2) hetero structure.  Owing to the fast plasma effects and meta stable hybrid phases, the TiCxN1-x is epitaxially grown on TiO2.  Energy band engineering at the interface induces high electron densities and a strong built-in elec. field, which lowers the Na+ diffusion barrier by a factor of 1.7.  As a result, the TiCxN1-x/N-TiO2 electrode exhibits excellent electrochem. performance.  The reversible specific capacities at rates of 0.1 and 10 C reach 312.3 and 173.7 mAh g-1, resp.  After 600 cycles of charge and discharge at 10 C, the capacity retention rate is 98.7%.  This work discovers an effective non-equil. plasma-enabled process to construct hetero interfaces that can enhance Na+ ion transport and provides generic guidelines for the design of hetero structures for a broader range of energy storage, sepn., and other devices that rely on controlled ionic transport.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpxQXyZKxacH7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li0e6M8u2dzIg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly Ordered Three-Dimensional Ni-TiO2 Nanoarrays as Sodium Ion Battery Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Yang; Zhou, Min; Wen, Liaoyong; Wang, Chengliang; Zhao, Huaping; Mi, Yan; Liang, Liying; Fu, Qun; Wu, Minghong; Lei, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIBs) represent an effective energy storage technol. with potentially lower material costs than Li ion batteries.  Here, the electrochem. performance of SIBs, esp. rate capability, is intimately connected to the electrode design at the nanoscale by taking anatase TiO2 as an example.  Highly ordered 3-dimensional (3D) Ni-TiO2 core-shell nanoarrays were fabricated using nanoimprited AAO templating technique and directly used as anode.  The nanoarrays delivered a reversible capacity of ∼200 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at the c.d. of 50 mA h g-1 and were able to retain a capacity of ∼95 mA h g-1 at the c.d. ≤5 A g-1 and fully recover low rate capacity.  High ion accessibility, fast electron transport, and excellent electrode integrity were shown as great merits to obtain the presented electrochem. performance.  The work demonstrates the possibility of highly ordered 3-dimensional heterostructured nanoarrays as a promising electrode design for Na energy storage to alleviate the reliance on the materials' intrinsic nature and provides a versatile and cost-effective technique for the fabrication of such perfectly ordered nanostructures.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoHslR0Alvw9bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgTJX9Gtdr8Sg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXpsFOjuro%253D&amp;md5=2843c505872489891b1e7f89f12fa7a3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2012.09.019"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bi, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Paranthaman, M.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-organized amorphous TiO2 nanotube arrays on porous Ti foam for rechargeable lithium and sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bi, Zhonghe; Paranthaman, M. Parans; Menchhofer, Paul A.; Dehoff, Ryan R.; Bridges, Craig A.; Chi, Miaofang; Guo, Bingkun; Sun, Xiao-Guang; Dai, Sheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">222</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Self-organized amorphous TiO2 nanotube arrays (NTAs) were successfully fabricated on both Ti foil and porous Ti foam through electrochem. anodization techniques.  The starting Ti foams were fabricated using ARCAM's Electron Beam Melting (EBM) technol.  The TiO2 NTAs on Ti foam were used as anodes in lithium ion batteries; they exhibited high capacities of 103 μAh cm-2 at 10 μA cm-2 and 83 μAh cm-2 at 500 μA cm-2, which are two to three times higher than those achieved on the std. Ti foil, which is around 40 μAh cm-2 at 10 μA cm-2 and 24 μAh cm-2 at 500 μA cm-2, resp.  This improvement is mainly attributed to higher surface area of the Ti foam and higher porosity of the nanotube arrays layer grown on the Ti foam.  In addn., a Na-ion half-cell composed of these NTAs anodes and Na metal as the counter electrode showed a self-improved specific capacity upon cycling at 10 μA cm-2.  These results indicate that TiO2 NTAs grown on Ti porous foam are promising electrodes for Li-ion or Na-ion rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrQoKGtXutC27Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgTJX9Gtdr8Sg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhsFSltrzL&amp;md5=3128b3e15618aaf7603602dc09540831</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1021/acs.jpcc.7b05675"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Chemical Origin of Termination-Functionalized MXenes: Ti3C2T2 as a Case Study</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Chemical Origin of Termination-Functionalized MXenes: Ti3C2T2 as a Case Study</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Tao; Li, Zhaojin; Hu, Minmin; Wang, Jiemin; Hu, Qingmiao; Li, Qingzhong; Wang, Xiaohui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">121</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">35</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors take Ti3C2T2 (T = O, F, OH, and H) as an example of MXenes, to demonstrate how termination stabilizes the Ti3C2 monolayer matrix by satg. the nonbonding valence electrons of the surface Ti atom by the low-energy orbitals of the termination.  This is achieved by orbitally resolved d. of states anal. by simply yet efficiently manipulating the internal coordination of the octahedral crystal field to match exactly the Cartesian coordination.  Highly degenerate 3d orbitals of surface Ti split in such a way that it exhibits pseudogaps whose widths predict a stability order Ti3C2O2 &gt; Ti3C2F2 &gt; Ti3C2(OH)2 &gt; Ti3C2H2 &gt; Ti3C2, consistent with Bader charge anal., thermodn. calcns., and exptl. results.  This new criterion could have implications in the general context of ubiquitous termination phenomena of MXenes and other relevant termination-functionalized 2D materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqlTTenYs60obVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgTJX9Gtdr8Sg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhtlCgu7jL&amp;md5=eb7ee27411f73b0a21af10ab61ca3b23</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1016/j.jechem.2020.05.002"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bao, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Amorphous nickel-cobalt bimetal-organic framework nanosheets with crystalline motifs enable efficient oxygen evolution reaction: Ligands hybridization engineering</span>. <i>J.
