                10.1016/j.jechem.2020.05.002</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D53%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D251-259%26journal%3DJ.%2BEnergy%2BChem.%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DZ.%2BGao%26author%3DH.%2BBao%26author%3DB.%2BZhang%26author%3DC.%2BWu%26author%3DC.%2BHuang%26author%3DZ.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BXie%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26title%3DAmorphous%2Bnickel-cobalt%2Bbimetal-organic%2Bframework%2Bnanosheets%2Bwith%2Bcrystalline%2Bmotifs%2Benable%2Befficient%2Boxygen%2Bevolution%2Breaction%253A%2BLigands%2Bhybridization%2Bengineering%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jechem.2020.05.002&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.2c01009&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jechem.2020.05.002&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Amorphous nickel-cobalt bimetal-organic framework nanosheets with crystalline motifs enable efficient oxygen evolution reaction: Ligands hybridization engineering</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yang; Gao, Zhonggui; Bao, Huiming; Zhang, Binghui; Wu, Cong; Huang, Chunfu; Zhang, Zilu; Xie, Yunyun; Wang, Hai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Energy Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">53</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">251-259</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JECOFG</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2095-4956</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Science Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Development of high-efficiency and low-cost electrocatalyst for oxygen evolution reaction (OER) is very important for use at alk. water electrolysis.  Metal-org. frameworks (MOF) provide a rich platform for designing multi-functional materials due to their controllable compn. and ultra-high surface area.  Herein, we report our findings in the development of amorphous nickel-cobalt bimetal-org. framework nanosheets with cryst. motifs via a simple "ligands hybridization engineering" strategy.  These complexes ' ligands contain inorg. ligands (H2O and NO-3) and org. ones, hexamethylenetetramine (HMT).  Further, we investigated a series of mixed-metal with multi-ligands materials as OER catalysts to explore their possible advantages and features.  It is found that the Ni doping is an effective approach for optimizing the electronic configuration, changing lattice ordering degree, and thus enhancing activities of HMT-based electrocatalysts.  Also, the cryst.-amorphous boundaries of various HMT-based electrocatalyst can be easily controlled by simply changing amts. of Ni-precursor added.  As a result, the optimized ultrathin (Co, 0.3Ni)-HMT nanosheets can reach a c.d. of 10 mA cm-2 at low overpotential of 330 mV with a small Tafel slope of 66 mV dec-1.  Our findings show that the electronic structure changes induced by Ni doping, 2D nanosheet structure, and MOF frameworks with multi-ligands compns. play crit. roles in the enhancement of the kinetically sluggish electrocatalytic OER.  The present study emphasizes the importance of ligands and active metals via hybridization for exploring novel efficient electrocatalysts.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGobz6xBgcYHM7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgTJX9Gtdr8Sg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Engineering the Interlayer Spacing by Pre-Intercalation for High Performance Supercapacitor MXene Electrodes in Room Temperature Ionic Liquid</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Kun; Matsumoto, Ray A.; Zhao, Wei; Osti, Naresh C.; Popov, Ivan; Thapaliya, Bishnu P.; Fleischmann, Simon; Misra, Sudhajit; Prenger, Kaitlyn; Tyagi, Madhusudan; Mamontov, Eugene; Augustyn, Veronica; Unocic, Raymond R.; Sokolov, Alexei P.; Dai, Sheng; Cummings, Peter T.; Naguib, Michael</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">MXenes exhibit excellent capacitance at high scan rates in sulfuric acid aq. electrolytes, but the narrow potential window of aq. electrolytes limits the energy d.  Org. electrolytes and room-temp. ionic liqs. (RTILs) can provide higher potential windows, leading to higher energy d.  The large cation size of RTIL hinders its intercalation in-between the layers of MXene limiting the specific capacitance in comparison to aq. electrolytes.  In this work, different chain lengths alkylammonium (AA) cations are intercalated into Ti3C2Tx, producing variation of MXene interlayer spacings (d-spacing).  AA-cation-intercalated Ti3C2Tx (AA-Ti3C2), exhibits higher specific capacitances, and cycling stabilities than pristine Ti3C2Tx in 1 M 1-ethly-3-methylimidazolium bis-(trifluoromethylsulfonyl)-imide (EMIMTFSI) in acetonitrile and neat EMIMTFSI RTIL electrolytes.  Pre-intercalated MXene with an interlayer spacing of ≈2.2 nm, can deliver a large specific capacitance of 257 F g-1 (1428 mF cm-2 and 492 F cm-3) in neat EMIMTFSI electrolyte leading to high energy d.  Quasi elastic neutron scattering and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy are used to study the dynamics of confined RTIL in pre-intercalated MXene.  Mol. dynamics simulations suggest significant differences in the structures of RTIL ions and AA cations inside the Ti3C2Tx interlayer, providing insights into the differences in the obsd. electrochem. behavior.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrS0xZXJt9KgrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgTJX9Gtdr8Sg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhsVens7vJ&amp;md5=4e84cb46b053f0162d8394a1df2bbc36</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1039/d0ta05151a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Activating an MXene as a host for EMIm+ by electrochemistry-driven Fe-ion pre-intercalation</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Activating an MXene as a host for EMIm+ by electrochemistry-driven Fe-ion pre-intercalation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Han, Wenjuan; Lu, Ming; Chen, Junnan; Li, Haojie; Li, Haibo; Zhang, Bingsen; Zhang, Wei; Zheng, Weitao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">EMIm+, as a substitute for Li+, can solve the initial problems that accompany lithiation/delithiation processes on an anode.  However, the larger size of EMIm+ limits the options when it comes to electrode materials.  Herein, a multilayered Ti3C2Tx MXene was electrochem. pre-intercalated with Fe ions to achieve EMIm+ hosting abilities.  As a result, a pre-intercalated MXene electrode exhibited enhanced EMIm+ transport and storage capabilities.  When integrated with an EMIm+[PF6]- ionic liq. electrolyte, the assembled DIB provides an energy d. of 76 W h kg-1 at a power d. of 360 W kg-1, and 94.3% of the energy d. is retained after 50 cycles.  Compared with a pristine example, the Fe pre-intercalated Ti3C2Tx MXene showed a significant increase in electrochem. performance.  Employing this approach to optimize layered materials may open up a new route for accurately tuning intercalated materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo7ntI5OcfoOLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liluKCaK95ICA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhtlymsb7O&amp;md5=f9012a9d0445d3b5932944ae6e6cb2ce</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1016/j.jechem.2021.08.001"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Status and challenges facing representative anode materials for rechargeable lithium batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Status and challenges facing representative anode materials for rechargeable lithium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Liqiang; Zhu, Chenxi; Yu, Sicheng; Ge, Daohan; Zhou, Haoshen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Energy Chemistry</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Rechargeable lithium batteries have been widely regarded as a revolutionary technol. to store renewable energy sources and extensively researched in the recent several decades.  As an indispensable part of lithium batteries, the evolution of anode materials has significantly promoted the development of lithium batteries.  However, since conventional lithium batteries with graphite anodes cannot meet the ever-increasing demands in different application scenarios (such as elec. vehicles and large-scale power supplies) which require high energy/power d. and long cycle life, various improvement strategies and alternative anode materials have been exploited for better electrochem. performance.  In this review, we detailedly introduced the characteristics and challenges of four representative anode materials for rechargeable lithium batteries, including graphite, Li4Ti5O12, silicon, and lithium metal.  And some of the latest advances are summarized, which mainly contain the modification strategies of anode materials and partially involve the optimization of electrode/electrolyte interface.  Finally, we make the conclusive comments and perspectives, and draw a development timeline on the four anode materials.  This review aims to offer a good primer for newcomers in the lithium battery field and benefit the structure and material design of anodes for advanced rechargeable lithium batteries in the future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoM3J06K8T9rbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liluKCaK95ICA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XisFers7bJ&amp;md5=c21bebdf702d3136a47dd8ba594f7bd7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202104730"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pulverization-Tolerant CuSe Nanoflakes with High (110) Planar Orientation for High-Performance Magnesium Storage</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pulverization-Tolerant CuSe Nanoflakes with High (110) Planar Orientation for High-Performance Magnesium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yuexing; Zhu, Youqi; Wang, Zhitao; Peng, Hui; Yang, Xinyu; Cao, Yuehua; Du, Changliang; Ma, Xilan; Cao, Chuanbao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">31</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">46</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2104730</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Copper chalcogenides are of great interest as conversion-type cathode materials due to their large specific capacity for rechargeable magnesium batteries, yet are subjected to severe capacity fading brought about by structure collapse in repetitive charge-discharge cycling.  Herein, single-cryst. and (110) preferentially oriented CuSe nanoflakes are designed via a temp.-controlled crystal growth route under microwave irradn.  The as-prepd. CuSe nanoflake cathode materials can present high reversible capacity (204 mAh g-1 at 200 mA g-1 c.d.), outstanding rate capability, and remarkable long-term cycling stability (≈0.095% capacity decay per cycle at 1 A g-1 within 700 cycles).  The multistep reversible conversion mechanism of the CuSe nanoflake cathode materials is evidenced by ex situ XPS and X-ray diffraction.  Structure evolution investigation suggests that the single-cryst. CuSe nanoflakes can exhibit relatively durable structural stability.  The desirable cycling stability can be ascribed to the excellent pulverization-tolerance of the CuSe nanoflake cathode materials endowed by the multistep reversible conversion mechanism and the single-cryst. feature.  Furthermore, the preferentially-oriented (110) active plane is favorable for electrochem. reactions to ensure high specific capacity.  This work can afford a crystal engineering strategy to fabricate high-performance conversion-type electrode materials for rechargeable magnesium batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp9awS7DfbmjLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liluKCaK95ICA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhsl2rsrnE&amp;md5=a5759c40cb3e0c90b12436df96d19f2c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1016/j.compositesb.2021.108733"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Boosting Li-storage properties of conversion-type anodes for lithium-ion batteries via steric effect of intercalation-type materials: A case of MnCO3†</span>. <i>Composites, Part B</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>212</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">108733</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.compositesb.2021.108733</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D212%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D108733%26journal%3DComposites%252C%2BPart%2BB%26author%3DJ.%2BSu%26author%3DZ.%2BGao%26author%3DY.%2BXie%26author%3DZ.%2BZhang%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26title%3DBoosting%2BLi-storage%2Bproperties%2Bof%2Bconversion-type%2Banodes%2Bfor%2Blithium-ion%2Bbatteries%2Bvia%2Bsteric%2Beffect%2Bof%2Bintercalation-type%2Bmaterials%253A%2BA%2Bcase%2Bof%2BMnCO3%25E2%2580%25A0%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.compositesb.2021.108733&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.2c01009&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.compositesb.2021.108733&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Boosting lithium-storage properties of conversion-type anodes for lithium-ion batteries through steric effect of intercalation-type materials and case of manganese carbonate</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Su, Jian; Gao, Zhonggui; Xie, Yunyun; Zhang, Zilu; Wang, Hai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Composites, Part B: Engineering</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">212</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">108733</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CPBEFF</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1359-8368</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The conversion-type anodes have been widely investigated in lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), due to their high theor. specific capacity.  However, their rate capability and cyclic stability were suffered from large vol. expansion and pulverization.  Herein, we report a method to improve the electrochem. performance of conversion-type anodes by using the steric effect of intercalation-type materials, as was done in conversion-type MnCO3.  The role of the intercalation-type TiO2 nanocrystals in the structural evolution of composite anodes was verified.  It was found that TiO2 nanocrystals could form a good elec. contact with as-pulverized MnCO3 anode, and maintain their structural stability.  Furthermore, the electrochem. anal. shows that TiO2 nanocrystals can provide fast electron transfer channels for the composites matrix, which is conducive to improving the rate capability of MnCO3 anode.  Moreover, TiO2 nanocrystals can effectively avoid the aggregation of metal Mn nanocrystals by their steric effect.  As a result, the composite anode showed better electrochem. properties than its counterpart MnCO3 by delivering 378 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 1 A g-1 after 200 cycles.  Different from previously reported methods, our strategy is simple and easy to scale.  Importantly, our research provides a new insight for solving issues involved vol. expansion and pulverization of conversion-type anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGobcv3Ek1W8xbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liluKCaK95ICA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXnt1Smsrk%253D&amp;md5=fc8bf4e2442c0ecf2a6e850ed2db28cc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1149/1945-7111/ab9404"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nickol, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Schied, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Heubner, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Schneider, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Michaelis, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bobeth, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cuniberti, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">GITT analysis of lithium insertion cathodes for determining the lithium diffusion coefficient at low temperature: challenges and pitfalls</span>. <i>J. Electrochem. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>167</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">090546</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1149/1945-7111/ab9404</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D167%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D090546%26journal%3DJ.%2BElectrochem.%2BSoc.%26author%3DA.%2BNickol%26author%3DT.%2BSchied%26author%3DC.%2BHeubner%26author%3DM.%2BSchneider%26author%3DA.%2BMichaelis%26author%3DM.%2BBobeth%26author%3DG.%2BCuniberti%26title%3DGITT%2Banalysis%2Bof%2Blithium%2Binsertion%2Bcathodes%2Bfor%2Bdetermining%2Bthe%2Blithium%2Bdiffusion%2Bcoefficient%2Bat%2Blow%2Btemperature%253A%2Bchallenges%2Band%2Bpitfalls%26doi%3D10.1149%252F1945-7111%252Fab9404&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.2c01009&amp;doiOfLink=10.1149%2F1945-7111%2Fab9404&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">GITT analysis of lithium insertion cathodes for determining the lithium diffusion coefficient at low temperature: challenges and pitfalls</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nickol, A.; Schied, T.; Heubner, C.; Schneider, M.; Michaelis, A.; Bobeth, M.; Cuniberti, G.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">167</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">090546</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JESOAN</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1945-7111</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">IOP Publishing Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Understanding the diffusion of lithium ions in electrode materials for lithium ion batteries is of great importance for their knowledge-based optimization and development of novel materials and cell designs.  The galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique (GITT) is widely applied in battery research to study the diffusion of lithium in anode and cathode materials depending on the degree of lithiation.  While transport properties of electrode materials at high and ambient temps. are largely available, low temp. diffusion and rate coeffs. are hardly reported in the literature and vary by orders of magnitude for identical active materials.  Herein, several challenges and pitfalls are demonstrated and discussed in the application and evaluation of GITT measurements for detg. the effective chem. lithium ion diffusion coeff. in lithium insertion electrodes, which become esp. important at low temp.  This includes theor. considerations and an exptl. anal. of the promising cathode material LiNi0.5Co0.2Mn0.3O2 (NCM523) in the wide temp. range of -40 to 40°.  The choice is shown of exptl. conditions for the GITT measurements and of the subsequent math. evaluation significantly affect the derived diffusion coeff.  The results suggest that the large scattering of reported values of the diffusion coeff. could be caused by the use of different evaluation procedures.  Simple calcn. methods appear to be less suited the lower the temp. is.  It is shown that the complementary use of GITT and EIS supplemented by detailed knowledge of the microstructure of the electrode significantly improves the accuracy of detg. the diffusion coeff.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqZ3KfYpBGHsLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhPhHSt9oiDNA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhvFSks7rP&amp;md5=b5a0680543e10d8badd85ada705a3933</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202109524"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Manipulating the Interlayer Spacing of 3D MXenes with Improved Stability and Zinc-Ion Storage Capability</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fabrication of Fe nanocomplex pillared few-layered Ti3C2Tx MXene with enhanced rate performance for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Pengfei; Zhang, Shunlong; Ying, Hangjun; Yang, Wentao; Wang, Jianli; Guo, Rongnan; Han, Weiqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1218-1227</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NRAEB5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1998-0000</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Abstr.: Pillaring technologies have been considered as an effective way to improve lithium storage performance of Ti3C2Tx MXene.  Nevertheless, the pillared hybrids suffer from sluggish Li+ diffusion kinetics and electronic transportation due to the compact multi-layered MXene structure, thus exhibiting inferior rate performance.  Herein, the few-layered Ti3C2 MXene (f-Ti3C2 MXene) which is free from restacking can be prepd. quickly based on the NH4+ ions method.  Besides, Fe nanocomplex pillared few-layered Ti3C2Tx (FPTC) heterostructures are fabricated via the intercalation of Fe ions into the interlayer of f-Ti3C2 MXene.  The f-Ti3C2 MXene which is immune to restacking can provide a highly conductive substrate for the rapid transport of Li+ ions and electrons and possess adequate electrolyte accessible area.  Consequently, the FPTC hybrids exhibit a high capacity of 535 mAh.g-1 after 150 cycles at 0.5 A.g-1 and an enhanced rate performance with 310 mAh.g-1 after 850 cycles at 5 A.g-1.  This strategy is facile, universal and can be extended to fabricate various few-layered MXene-derived hybrids with superior rate capability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqvA5wM06l_k7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhPhHSt9oiDNA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhtV2itrzF&amp;md5=56bcf65880fb911c90dc240ada0f0192</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1002/admi.201902008"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Riazi, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Anayee, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hantanasirisakul, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shamsabadi, A.                         "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.10.033"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.-C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, J.-N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.-P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, A.-H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Designed synthesis of nitrogen-rich carbon wrapped Sn nanoparticles hybrid anode via in-situ growth of crystalline ZIF-8 on a binary metal oxide</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>19</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">486</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">494</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.10.033</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D19%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D486-494%26journal%3DNano%2BEnergy%26author%3DF.%2BCheng%26author%3DW.-C.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.-N.%2BZhu%26author%3DW.-P.%2BZhang%26author%3DA.-H.%2BLu%26title%3DDesigned%2Bsynthesis%2Bof%2Bnitrogen-rich%2Bcarbon%2Bwrapped%2BSn%2Bnanoparticles%2Bhybrid%2Banode%2Bvia%2Bin-situ%2Bgrowth%2Bof%2Bcrystalline%2BZIF-8%2Bon%2Ba%2Bbinary%2Bmetal%2Boxide%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.nanoen.2015.10.033&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.2c01009&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.nanoen.2015.10.033&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Designed synthesis of nitrogen-rich carbon wrapped Sn nanoparticles hybrid anode via in-situ growth of crystalline ZIF-8 on a binary metal oxide</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cheng, Fei; Li, Wen-Cui; Zhu, Jian-Nan; Zhang, Wei-Ping; Lu, An-Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">19</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">486-494</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We have established a novel and solvent-free synthesis of superior performance Sn/C anode derived from binary metal oxides which initiated the outward growth of ZIF-8 approach.  The obtained anode has highly dispersed Sn nanoparticles wrapped in nitrogen-rich carbon with a 3D continuous conductive framework and a high Sn content of 82.3 wt% Binary metal oxide (ZnSnO3) is chosen together with imidazole to direct ZIF-8 growing around tin oxides according to the theory of hard and soft acids and bases.  This ensures an encapsulation of tin oxides with high dispersion into ZIF-8.  Subsequent pyrolysis allows the outward growth of ZIF-8 convert into a continuous and nitrogen-rich (5.3 wt%) carbon network with good cond.  Meanwhile, tin oxides are reduced to Sn nanoparticles by carbothermal redn. and the reduced zinc consequently evaps. to create open pores which contribute to fast transportation of lithium-ions and electrons.  Consequently, the Sn/C anode presents an initial discharge capacity of 1321 mA h g-1 with superior coulombic efficiency of 80.1% at 0.2 A g-1.  Reversible capacities of 901 mA h g-1 at 0.2 A g-1 and 690 mA h g-1 at 1 A g-1 are reserved after 150 cycles.  Importantly, this designed synthesis suggests a new approach to produce other materials such as MnO/C anode exhibiting good performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrpkvpCNiGvOLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhPhHSt9oiDNA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVaqtrvM&amp;md5=1f758642b6c8f7238d43cf31a6406b5e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1016/S0926-3373(03)00075-4"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Araña, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dona-Rodrıguez, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rendón, E.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Plasma-induced conversion of polystyrene nanoplastics in water: Intermediates release, toxicity, and disinfection byproducts formation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Liling; Wang, Ruigang; Liu, Yue; Zhang, Ying; Zhou, Jian; Qu, Guangzhou; Tang, Shoufeng; Wang, Tiecheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">433</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">Part_1</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Widely distributed nanoplastics have become a threat to water environment.  Information regarding their conversion behaviors and risks under oxidn. conditions is still lacking.  In this study, conversion of polystyrene nanoplastics (PSNPs) in water induced by elec. plasma was investigated, and its risks were evaluated in terms of Scenedesmus obliquus growth, Human alveolar cell A549 toxicity, and chlorinated disinfection byproducts (DBPs) formation.  Attacks of 1O2 and ·OH resulted in rough surface, smaller particle size of PSNPs (particles larger than 200 nm disappeared, and it was in the range of 50-150 nm), sequence breakages in functional groups, and generation of hydroxylated and carboxylated intermediates.  The plasma-treated PSNPs exhibited slightly weaker toxicity for Scenedesmus obliquus growth when PSNPs concn. was 30 mg L-1, but stronger toxicity for A549 (relative viability of A549 decreased from approx. 40% to 6.9% after 15 min treatment).  The hydroxylated and carboxylated intermediates were important precursors of DBPs, and the formation potentials and toxicities of haloacetic acid DBPs increased with the plasma treatment.  The relevant roadmaps among haloacetic acid DBPs and conversion intermediates were figured out.  Overall, the conversion of PSNPs under oxidn. exposure may pose a greater threat to DBPs formation, which deserved more attention.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGokXyBLSTZKDLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljtRSktVvrcaQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XpvFSjsA%253D%253D&amp;md5=2fbbd3f479116f87966b6f4459e050a8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1016/j.molstruc.2005.06.003"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Seoudi, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">El-Bahy, G.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The IR spectra of phthalocyanine and (Mg+2, Mn+2, Fe+2, Co+2, Zn+2 and Pb+2) phthalocyanines were studied using FTIR in the range from (4000-400 cm-1), as halide disks.  The absorption bands of phthalocyanines were compared with the spectral data of phthalocyanine and discussed in relation to its structure.  The N-H bands appearing at 3289 and 1006 cm-1 in phthalocyanine disappeared in the phthalocyanines.  This is due to the replacement of H by the metal cation.  A new band appeared at 1050 cm-1 in the metal phthalocyanines, which may be due to the inactive C-N vibration in phthalocyanine activated by the complex formation.  Thermogravimetric (TG) anal. curves show that, the main degrdn. step follows 1st order kinetics.  The minor and major decompn. temp. and also the activation energy of the main degrdn. step was calcd. and discussed.  This study focuses on the correlation existing between the structure and the continuous dark cond. in compacted powder.  The temp. dependence of the cond. was measured in the range (283-450 K) and hints at an activated-like behavior with activation energies depending on the structure.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">FT-IR and Raman spectroscopic study of Fenugreek (Trigonella foenum graecum L.) seeds</span></div><div class="casAuthors">El-Bahy, G. M. S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Applied Spectroscopy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2005</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">72</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">111-116</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The compn. of Fenugreek seeds in the form of powder, ash, and oil is investigated through FT-IR and FT Raman spectra measurements.  The results indicate that Fenugreek seeds (powder) are rich in proteins.  Fats (lipids) and starch are present in small amts. in the seeds.  The FT-IR absorption bands of seed powder appeared at: 3365 cm-1 assigned as N-H stretching vibrations (amide A of protein), 1657 cm-1 (C=O, amide I), 1540 cm-1 (N-H bending vibration, amide II), and 1240 cm-1 (N-H bending, amide III).  In the FT Raman spectra the band at 1661 cm-1 is ascribed to amide I ν(C=O) of proteins while the band at 1080 cm-1 indicates the starch.  The fenugreek oil Fourier transform IR absorbance ratios A(3009 cm-1)/A(2924 cm-1), A(3009 cm-1)/A(2854 cm-1), and A(3009 cm-1)/A(1740 cm-1) were considered for measuring the iodine values.  These ratios (0.3609, 0.4916, and 0.4129) revealed that the iodine value of fenugreek oil is higher than that of other oils.  On the other hand, the ash of fenugreek is very rich in phosphate compds.  The spectra showed absorption bands at frequencies 1082, 1000, 618, and 566 cm-1, and the FT Raman spectrum showed a strong absorbance band at 793 cm-1, which is due to phosphate compds.  It could be concluded that the inorg. part of fenugreek consists mainly of phosphate compds.  The Fenugreek seed contains proteins, fat, fiber, and ash, which is in complete harmony with AACC, 1980.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo8SeaR1WLVLrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljtRSktVvrcaQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2MXjvVWisb8%253D&amp;md5=f915ade98ac1492e0d9c96bb07bdcb23</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1016/j.sna.2021.112839"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gupta, L.                         cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Intense Raman D Band without Disorder in Flattened Carbon Nanotubes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Picheau, Emmanuel; Impellizzeri, Anthony; Rybkovskiy, Dmitry; Bayle, Maxime; Mevellec, Jean-Yves; Hof, Ferdinand; Saadaoui, Hassan; Noe, Laure; Torres Dias, Abraao Cefas; Duvail, Jean-Luc; Monthioux, Marc; Humbert, Bernard; Puech, Pascal; Ewels, Christopher P.; Penicaud, Alain</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Above a crit. diam., single- or few-walled carbon nanotubes spontaneously collapse as flattened carbon nanotubes.  Raman spectra of isolated flattened and cylindrical carbon nanotubes have been recorded.  The collapse provokes an intense and narrow D band, despite the absence of any lattice disorder.  The curvature change near the edge cavities activates a D band, despite framework continuity.  Theor. calcns. based on Placzek approxn. fully corroborate this exptl. finding.  Usually used as a tool to quantify defect d. in graphenic structures, the D band cannot be used as such in the presence of a graphene fold.  This conclusion should serve as a basis to revisit materials comprising structural distortion where poor carbon organization was concluded on a Raman basis.  Our finding also emphasizes the different visions of a defect between chemists and physicists, a possible source of confusion for researchers working in nanotechnologies.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrScHi8EdtXWbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgh6IRAVDqmRA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhtFCjsL0%253D&amp;md5=6c1f7d0672e47e0ba0889d9da1200b95</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref55'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit55" data-doi="10.1007/s10853-021-06283-5"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kato, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yamada, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nishikawa, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Otomo, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sato, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sato, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Origins of peaks of graphitic and pyrrolic nitrogen in N1s X-ray photoelectron spectra of carbon materials: quaternary nitrogen, tertiary amine, or secondary amine?</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Origins of peaks of graphitic and pyrrolic nitrogen in N1s X-ray photoelectron spectra of carbon materials: quaternary nitrogen, tertiary amine, or secondary amine</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kato, Tomofumi; Yamada, Yasuhiro; Nishikawa, Yasushi; Otomo, Toshiya; Sato, Hayato; Sato, Satoshi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">56</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">28</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">15798-15811</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMTSAS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0022-2461</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">XPS is among the most powerful techniques to analyze structures of nitrogen-doped carbon materials.  However, reported assignments of (1) graphitic nitrogen (N)/substitutional N, quaternary N (Q-N), or tertiary amine (T-N) and (2) pyrrolic N/secondary amine or T-N are questionable.  Most reports assign peaks at ca. 401 eV as Q-N or graphitic N, whereas raw materials in most of those works contain neither counter anion nor halogen.  Besides, the peak at ca. 400 eV has been assigned as pyrrolic N, but the presence of N-H is generally not confirmed.  In this work, it was clarified that one of the reasons for the prevailing ambiguous assignments is the presence of N in heptagonal and pentagonal rings.  The peaks at 400.1-401.2 eV were detd. to be T-N, but not Q-N by analyzing graphitized polyimide (with the oxygen content of 0.01 at% or lower and the hydrogen content of 0 at%) using Raman spectroscopy, XPS, X-ray diffraction, total neutron scattering, elemental anal., and mol. dynamics simulation.  Besides, it was revealed that the peak at 400.1 eV originated from T-N on 5-membered rings or 7- and 5-membered rings, but not pyrrolic N because graphite including no hydrogen was used for anal.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpZFm3HFJjfBrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgh6IRAVDqmRA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhsFGgs7nF&amp;md5=dcab29bc0d0a69fbf5f4b61011527da1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref56'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit56" data-doi="10.1016/j.apcatb.2018.07.038"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komatsuda, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Asakura, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Vequizo, J. J. M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yamakata, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enhanced photocatalytic NO decomposition of visible-light responsive F-TiO2/(N,C)-TiO2 by charge transfer between F-TiO2 and (N,C)-TiO2 through their doping levels</span>. <i>Appl.                 10.1016/j.apcatb.2018.07.038</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D238%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D358-364%26journal%3DAppl.%2BCatal.%252C%2BB%26author%3DS.%2BKomatsuda%26author%3DY.%2BAsakura%26author%3DJ.%2BJ.%2BM.%2BVequizo%26author%3DA.%2BYamakata%26author%3DS.%2BYin%26title%3DEnhanced%2Bphotocatalytic%2BNO%2Bdecomposition%2Bof%2Bvisible-light%2Bresponsive%2BF-TiO2%252F%2528N%252CC%2529-TiO2%2Bby%2Bcharge%2Btransfer%2Bbetween%2BF-TiO2%2Band%2B%2528N%252CC%2529-TiO2%2Bthrough%2Btheir%2Bdoping%2Blevels%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.apcatb.2018.07.038&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.2c01009&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.apcatb.2018.07.038&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit56R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">56</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced photocatalytic NOx decomposition of visible-light responsive F-TiO2/(N,C)-TiO2 by charge transfer between F-TiO2 and (N,C)-TiO2 through their doping levels</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Komatsuda, Shio; Asakura, Yusuke; Vequizo, Junie Jhon M.; Yamakata, Akira; Yin, Shu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Applied Catalysis, B: Environmental</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">238</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Composite type photocatalyst F-TiO2/(N,C)-TiO2 consisted of anatase-type TiO2 with fluorine-doping (F-TiO2) and TiO2 with nitrogen and carbon-doping ((N,C)-TiO2) was prepd. by simple phys. mixing to exhibit higher visible-light responsive photocatalytic nitrogen oxide (NOx) decompn. activity than those of F-TiO2 and (N,C)-TiO2.  Transient absorption measurement clarified that the composite possessed longer carrier lifetime compared to that of each material (F-TiO2 or (N,C)-TiO2), resulting in higher photocatalytic activity.  In the composite, photoexcited holes and electrons, which are not in impurity level but in valence and conduction band, resp., should photocatalytically decomp. NOx, judging from the redox potential of O2/O -2 and the band positions of F-TiO2 and (N,C)-TiO2.  The mechanism for higher visible-light photocatalytic activity, or longer carrier lifetime can be explained by charge transfer between F-TiO2 and (N,C)-TiO2 through their impurity levels.  The charge transfer should make photoexcited carries spatially sepd. to enhance the photocatalytic activity.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp4cyKf7OIP2rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgh6IRAVDqmRA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtlKmtrnM&amp;md5=75981cead6bf4bfa0df950b5cb9da697</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref57'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit57" data-doi="10.1039/c0jm03873c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">TiO2(B)@carbon composite nanowires as anode for lithium ion batteries with enhanced reversible capacity and cyclic performance</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit57R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">57</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">TiO2(B)@carbon composite nanowires as anode for lithium ion batteries with enhanced reversible capacity and cyclic performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Zunxian; Du, Guodong; Guo, Zaiping; Yu, Xuebin; Chen, Zhixin; Guo, Tailiang; Liu, Huakun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Novel TiO2(B)@carbon composite nanowires were prepd. by a 2-step hydrothermal process with subsequent heat treatment in Ar.  The nanostructures exhibit the unique feature of having TiO2(B) encapsulated inside and an amorphous C layer coating the outside.  The unique core/shell structure and chem. compn. is likely to lead to perfect performance in many applications.  The results of Li-ion battery testing are presented to demonstrate the superior cyclic performance and rate capability of the TiO2(B)@carbon nanowires.  The composite nanowires exhibit a high reversible capacity of 560 mA-h/g after 100 cycles at the c.d. of 30 mA/g and excellent cycling stability and rate capability (200 mA-h/g when cycled at the c.d. of 750 mA/g), indicating that the composite is a promising anode material for Li-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq8KzycTCkeMbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgh6IRAVDqmRA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXntVOrurk%253D&amp;md5=28ae5d53654404f52379c25dccdfe35b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref58"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref58'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">58</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit58" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201902547"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, R.                         cas_cit58R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">58</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">N/O Dual-Doped Environment-Friendly Hard Carbon as Advanced Anode for Potassium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cui, Rong Chao; Xu, Bo; Dong, Hou Ji; Yang, Chun Cheng; Jiang, Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Science (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1902547</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ASDCCF</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2198-3844</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) are considered as promising candidates for lithium-ion batteries due to the abundant reserve and lower cost of K resources.  However, K+ exhibits a larger radius than that of Li+, which may impede the intercalation of K+ into the electrode, thus resulting in poor cycling stability of PIBs.  Here, an N/O dual-doped hard carbon (NOHC) is constructed by carbonizing the renewable piths of sorghum stalks.  As a PIB anode, NOHC presents a high reversible capacity (304.6 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 after 100 cycles) and superior cycling stability (189.5 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 5000 cycles).  The impressive electrochem. performances can be ascribed to the super-stable porous structure, expanded interlayer space, and N/O dual-doping.  More importantly, the NOHC can be prepd. in large scale in a concise way, showing great potential for commercialization applications.  This work may impel the development of low-cost and sustainable carbon-based materials for PIBs and other advanced energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqUwW_pH6nwtrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhbLLdgRPc0Pw"> &gt;&gt; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>;                         cas_cit60R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">60</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">TiO2-Based Heterostructures with Different Mechanism: A General Synergistic Effect toward High-Performance Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Man; Chu, Yanting; Xi, Baojuan; Shi, Nianxiang; Duan, Bin; Zhang, Chenghui; Chen, Weihua; Feng, Jinkui; Xiong, Shenglin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2004054</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1613-6810</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The general synergistic effect of TiO2-based heterostructures has been discovered to improve the sodium storage of anodes, involving conversion, alloying, and insertion mechanism materials.  Herein, metal sulfides (MS2, M = Sn2+, Co2+, Mo2+), metallic Sb and Sn, as well as, carbon nanotubes (CNTs) are chosen as the model examples from the three kinds.  The electrochem. testing demonstrates a better performance of heterostructrues involving TiO2 than the pristine anode components.  The introduction of TiO2 into the MS2 and Sb or Sn systems induces a built-in elec. field as the charge transfer force at the heterojunctions, greatly reducing the ion transfer resistance and promoting interfacial electron transfer.  In the CNT/TiO2 structure, the chem. growth of TiO2 nanoparticles on the outer surface of CNTs makes the interface more compact than the phys. blending case, offering better improvement of electrochem.  The synergy should work via the growth of heterostructures, relying on the interface effects, which always plays the promotion role through the formation of driving force or grain boundaries and/or condense phase interface to facilitate charge transfer at the interface during the storage process.  Therefore, the construction of reasonable heterostructures can endow materials with intriguing electrochem. performance based on the synergistic effect.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a Yahia, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Vergnet, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Saubanère, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Doublet, M.-L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Unified picture of anionic redox in Li/Na-ion batteries</span>. <i>Nat. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>18</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">496</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">502</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/s41563-019-0318-3</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unified picture of anionic redox in Li/Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ben Yahia, Mouna; Vergnet, Jean; Saubanere, Matthieu; Doublet, Marie-Liesse</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">18</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">496-502</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NMAACR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1476-1122</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Research</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Anionic redox in Li-rich and Na-rich transition metal oxides (A-rich-TMOs) has emerged as a new paradigm to increase the energy d. of rechargeable batteries.  Ever since, numerous electrodes delivering extra anionic capacity beyond the theor. cationic capacity have been reported.  Unfortunately, most often the anionic capacity achieved in charge is partly irreversible in discharge.  A unified picture of anionic redox in A-rich-TMOs is designed here to identify the electronic origin of this irreversibility and to propose new directions to improve the cycling performance of the electrodes.  The electron localization function is introduced as a holistic tool to unambiguously locate the O lone pairs in the structure and follow their participation in the redox activity of A-rich-TMOs.  The charge-transfer gap of transition metal oxides is proposed as the pertinent observable to quantify the amt. of extra capacity achievable in charge and its reversibility in discharge, irresp. of the material chem. compn.  From this generalized approach, the reversibility of the anionic capacity is limited to a crit. no. of O holes per O, hO ≤ 1/3.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpNxw9BVJtqRbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0limlxekTJSu4Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXmslans7Y%253D&amp;md5=7a52af474fdbf2a6e1b7b38d0addd2bb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1038/natrevmats.2018.13"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Vaalma, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Buchholz, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Weil, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Passerini, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A cost and resource analysis of sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Nat.                 10.1038/natrevmats.2018.13</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have captured widespread attention for grid-scale energy storage owing to the natural abundance of sodium.  The performance of such batteries is limited by available electrode materials, esp. for sodium-ion layered oxides, motivating the exploration of high compositional diversity.  How the compn. dets. the structural chem. is decisive for the electrochem. performance but very challenging to predict, esp. for complex compns.  The "cationic potential" is introduced that captures the key interactions of layered materials and makes it possible to predict the stacking structures.  This is demonstrated through the rational design and prepn. of layered electrode materials with improved performance.  As the stacking structure dets. the functional properties, this methodol. offers a soln. toward the design of alkali metal layered oxides.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqSJI5LmdJYXbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liK1EA_NKQeSw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXit1Kru7fI&amp;md5=979fa3c7f742539bf50f3e5dea98b16a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202001852"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chou, S.                         rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electron Delocalization and Dissolution-Restraint in Vanadium Oxide Superlattices to Boost Electrochemical Performance of Aqueous Zinc-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Weijie; Han, Chao; Gu, Qinfen; Chou, Shu-Lei; Wang, Jia-Zhao; Liu, Hua-Kun; Dou, Shi-Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Aq. zinc-ion batteries (ZIBs) have triggered a great deal of scientific research and become a promising alternative for large-scale energy storage applications, owing to the unique merits of high volumetric energy d., abundance of zinc resources, eco-friendliness, and safety.  The pace of progress of ZIB development, however, is hindered by their poor reversibility and sluggish kinetics, derived from the dissoln. of active materials in aq. electrolytes and the strong electrostatic interactions between Zn2+ and the cathode lattice.  Herein, a vanadium oxide (V2O5-x)/polyaniline (PANI-V) superlattice structure is demonstrated as a model of superlattice structural engineering to overcome these weaknesses.  In this superlattice, the PANI layer not only plays the role of a spacer to expand the V2O5-x interlayer spacing but also serves as a conductive capacity contributor.  Moreover, the PANI layer servers as structural stabilizer to restrain the dissoln. of V2O5-x active materials in aq. electrolytes.  In addn., it introduces an interface effect to modulate the charge distribution of the V2O5-x monolayer, promoting Zn-ion diffusion into the structure.  Correspondingly, weakening the electrostatic interactions and suppressing the active materials dissoln. synergistically boosts the electrochem. performance for Zn-ion storage.  This work paves the way for the development/improvement of cathodes for aq. zinc-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo58cbjE89UwrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liK1EA_NKQeSw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXitlaitr%252FP&amp;md5=0f319a65e5476f5c427a8cab938bc007</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202001633"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bak, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shadike, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Waluyo, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hunt, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Senanayake, S.                         rightTab-cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The Role of Electron Localization in Covalency and Electrochemical Properties of Lithium-Ion Battery Cathode Materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xuelong; Fan, Xiulin; Yu, Xiqian; Bak, Seongmin; Shadike, Zulipiya; Waluyo, Iradwikanari; Hunt, Adrian; Senanayake, Sanjaya D.; Li, Hong; Chen, Liquan; Wang, Chunsheng; Xiao, Ruijuan; Hu, Enyuan; Yang, Xiao-Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Following the fundamental research conducted by J.B. Goodenough, the important role of electron localization induced by elemental substitution is studied.  The size and electron negativity of host and substituting ions are two important factors in tuning material properties such as local structure and transition metal (TM) oxygen covalency.  However, another factor, electron localization, which is widely studied in catalyst research but largely overlooked for battery materials, deserves systematic studies.  A combined investigation using synchrotronbased X-ray spectroscopy and theor. calcns. is carried out on the Li-Co-Mn-O model system in which the substituting cation Mn4+, with its 3d3 electronic structure, is used as a promoter for electron localization.  Results indicate that electron localization greatly influences the Co-O bond by making it less covalent, which increases the delithiation voltage.  It is also found that during charge/discharge, electron localization tends to make TM K-edge X-ray absorption near edge spectroscopy (XANES) spectra show a more ''rigid shift'' behavior while electron delocalization makes the XANES exhibit a ''shape change.''.  It clearly explains why the K-edge XANES data of some TM oxides show no ''rigid shift'' while the nominal valence states changed.  This work highlights the importance of electron localization with guidance for XANES interpretation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqSCkyH3pYr-bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liK1EA_NKQeSw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXptlelsLg%253D&amp;md5=88aa5b3b59ba70a8f04749394d21e1a6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1038/s41563-018-0098-1"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Aubrey, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Conductive metal-org. frameworks are an emerging class of three-dimensional architectures with degrees of modularity, synthetic flexibility and structural predictability that are unprecedented in other porous materials.  However, engendering long-range charge delocalization and establishing synthetic strategies that are broadly applicable to the diverse range of structures encountered for this class of materials remain challenging.  Here, we report the synthesis of KxFe2(BDP)3 (0 ≤ x ≤ 2; BDP2- = 1,4-benzenedipyrazolate), which exhibits full charge delocalization within the parent framework and charge mobilities comparable to technol. relevant polymers and ceramics.  Through a battery of spectroscopic methods, computational techniques and single-microcrystal field-effect transistor measurements, we demonstrate that fractional redn. of Fe2(BDP)3 results in a metal-org. framework that displays a nearly 10,000-fold enhancement in cond. along a single crystallog. axis.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Confronted with challenges in promoting fast AlxCly- anion diffusion and intercalation for aluminum ion batteries (AIBs), it is of vital importance to rationally design gradient hetero-interfaces with an ideal built-in interfacial elec. potential to enhance charge diffusion and transfer kinetics.  Herein, we demonstrate an effective strategy to realize accurate tuning gradient heteroatom N and P doping in MOF-derived porous carbon in C@N-C@N,P-C graded heterostructures.  Importantly, gradient N and P doping could modify the electronic structure of MOF-derived carbon as certified by DFT calcns., and lead to charge redistribution to induce graded energy levels and a built-in elec. field in the C@N-C@N,P-C graded heteroat. interface, thus boosting interfacial charge transfer and accelerating reaction kinetics.  Furthermore, the large surface area and high porosity of C@N-C@N,P-C graded heterostructures could efficiently absorb electrolyte and enhance anion transport kinetics.  As expected, the designed gradiently N,P-doped C@N-C@N,P-C heterostructure with a built-in interfacial elec. field could facilitate electron and AlCl4- anion transfer spontaneously between N,P-C, N-C and C gradient components, exhibiting a superior capacity of 98 mA h g-1 at a high c.d. of 5 A g-1 after 2500 cycles.
